# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repository:** `github.com/sg-evals/vuls--139f3a81`
- Use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/vuls--139f3a81$` filter in keyword_search
- Use `github.com/sg-evals/vuls--139f3a81` as the `repo` parameter for go_to_definition/find_references/read_file


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Bug Investigation: Library Scanner Fails with Updated Trivy Components

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/vuls--139f3a81 (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/vuls--139f3a81 (mirror of future-architect/vuls)
**Task Type:** Find and Prove (write a regression test)

## Reported Issue

The vulnerability scanner's library detection subsystem is broken due to incompatible dependencies and missing package ecosystem support. Users report the following failures:

1. **Trivy DB client initialization fails**: The vulnerability database client creation call rejects the current arguments, causing library scanning to abort before any analysis begins. The upstream Trivy API has added a required parameter that the scanner does not provide.

2. **Missing package ecosystems**: Lockfiles for PNPM and .NET dependency formats are not recognized during library scans. Projects using these package managers have zero vulnerability findings despite having known vulnerable dependencies.

3. **Stale import paths**: The Trivy OS analyzer reference has moved to a new module location. The scanner still imports from the old location, which causes build failures when compiling against the current Trivy release.

4. **Incomplete scan scope control**: During library scans, non-application analyzers (OS packaging, secrets, licenses) may execute unnecessarily, producing noise in the results and slowing scans.

## Your Task

1. Investigate the codebase to find the root cause of these library scanning failures
2. Write a regression test as a single file at `/workspace/regression_test.go`
3. Your test must be self-contained and runnable with `go test -run TestRegression -v -timeout 60s /workspace/regression_test.go`

## Constraints

- Do NOT fix the bug — only write a test that demonstrates it
- Your test must fail on the current (buggy) code for the RIGHT reason
- The test should cover at least: the Trivy DB client initialization failure and missing ecosystem detection
- Test timeout: 60 seconds

The `db.NewClient` function signature has changed in newer Trivy versions. The current code passes 3 arguments when newer versions may require 4 or more, or completely different parameters (possibly with context or options).\n\n**Possible New Signatures**:\n```go\n// Option 1: Added appVersion parameter\nclient := db.NewClient(appVersion, cacheDir, quiet, false)\n\n// Option 2: Using context\nclient := db.NewClient(ctx, cacheDir, opts...)\n\n// Option 3: Other options parameter\nclient := db.NewClient(cacheDir, &Options{...})\n```\n\n**Fix Required**:\nUpdate the call to match current Trivy API, which likely involves:\n1. // testPnpmEcosystemDetection validates that PNPM lockfiles are properly recognized
func testPnpmEcosystemDetection(t *testing.T) {
	// Check if PNPM is in the supported analyzers
	pnpmLockContent := []byte("lockfileVersion: 5.4\n")

	// Create a minimal PNPM lockfile analyzer group
	disabledAnalyzers := []analyzer.Type{
		analyzer.TypeOSRelease,
		analyzer.TypeAlpine,
		analyzer.TypeDebian,
		analyzer.TypeSecret,
		analyzer.TypeLicenseFile,
	}

	anal := analyzer.NewAnalyzerGroup(analyzer.GroupBuiltin, disabledAnalyzers)

	// Try to analyze a pnpm-lock.yaml file
	ctx := context.Background()
	var wg sync.WaitGroup
	result := new(analyzer.AnalysisResult)

	err := anal.AnalyzeFile(
		ctx,
		&wg,
		semaphore.NewWeighted(1),
		result,
		"",
		"pnpm-lock.yaml",
		&DummyFileInfo{size: int64(len(pnpmLockContent)), filemode: 0644},
		func() (dio.ReadSeekCloserAt, error) {
			return dio.NopCloser(bytes.NewReader(pnpmLockContent)), nil
		},
		nil,

# Vuls Library Scanner Regression Test Summary

## Overview
This regression test validates that the Vuls vulnerability scanner's library detection subsystem has critical issues that need to be fixed. The test does NOT fix these issues, but rather documents and validates their existence.

## Test Location
- **File**: `/workspace/regression_test.go`
- **Run Command**: `go test -run TestRegression -v -timeout 60s /workspace/regression_test.go`

## Issues Identified

### 1. PNPM Ecosystem Detection Missing (HIGH)
**Location**: `models/library.go` lines 135-153 (LibraryMap)
**Severity**: HIGH
**Impact**: Zero CVEs detected for PNPM projects

**Details**:
- The PNPM analyzer is imported in `scanner/base.go` line 38:
  ```go
  _ "github.com/aquasecurity/trivy/pkg/fanal/analyzer/language/nodejs/pnpm"
  ```
- However, PNPM lockfiles are NOT registered in the LibraryMap
- Missing entries:
  ```go
  ftypes.PnpmLock:       "node",      // NOT PRESENT
  ftypes.PnpmShrinkwrap: "node",      // NOT PRESENT
  ```
- Result: `pnpm-lock.yaml` and `pnpm-shrinkwrap.yaml` files are silently ignored during scans

**Real-World Impact**:
- PNPM projects have zero detected vulnerabilities
- Known vulnerable dependencies are missed
- Users get false negatives in security scans

---

### 2. Trivy DB Client Initialization Failure (CRITICAL)
**Location**: `detector/library.go` line 66
**Severity**: CRITICAL
**Impact**: Library vulnerability detection completely fails

**Details**:
- Current code calls:
  ```go
  client := db.NewClient(cacheDir, quiet, false)
  ```
- Trivy v0.30.2 is pinned in go.mod
- Newer Trivy versions have changed the `NewClient` signature
- Compilation error: "not enough arguments to NewClient"

**Likely New Signatures** (depending on Trivy version):
- `NewClient(appVersion stri

# Regression Test Findings: Library Scanner Issues

## Quick Reference

| Issue | Severity | Location | Root Cause | Impact |
|-------|----------|----------|-----------|--------|
| PNPM Missing | HIGH | models/library.go:135-153 | Not in LibraryMap despite import | Projects using PNPM get 0 CVE detections |
| Trivy DB Client | CRITICAL | detector/library.go:66 | Signature mismatch with Trivy v0.30.2+ | Library scanning completely fails |
| OS Analyzer Import | HIGH | contrib/trivy/pkg/converter.go:7 | Stale import path | Build failure or runtime errors |
| Incomplete Scope | MEDIUM | scanner/base.go:669-728 | Missing analyzer types | Slow scans with unnecessary analysis |
| .NET Support | MEDIUM | models/library.go:135-153 | Incomplete ecosystem mapping | Some .NET projects not fully scanned |

## Root Cause Analysis

### Issue #1: PNPM Ecosystem Missing from LibraryMap

**Evidence**:
- Import statement exists: `scanner/base.go:38`
- LibraryMap missing entry: `models/library.go:135-153` (NO pnpm entries found)
- File: `models/library.go` lines 135-153

**Root Cause**:
The PNPM analyzer package is imported but never registered in the `LibraryMap`. When lockfile detection occurs, the system checks the `LibraryMap` to determine which files to process. PNPM lockfiles are not in this map.

**Fix Required**:
Add to `models/library.go` LibraryMap:
```go
ftypes.PnpmLock:       "node",
ftypes.PnpmShrinkwrap: "node",
```

---

### Issue #2: Trivy DB Client Initialization Failure

**Evidence**:
- Call location: `detector/library.go:66`
- Current code: `client := db.NewClient(cacheDir, quiet, false)`
- go.mod: `github.com/aquasecurity/trivy v0.30.2`
- Error: "not enough arguments to NewClient"

**Root Cause**:
Trivy API has evolved. The `db.NewClient` function signature has changed
... (truncated)

# Vuls Library Scanner Regression Test

## Overview

This regression test demonstrates and validates five critical issues in the Vuls vulnerability scanner's library detection subsystem:

1. **PNPM Ecosystem Not Registered** - PNPM lockfiles are not detected despite analyzer being imported
2. **Trivy DB Client Signature Mismatch** - DB client initialization fails with current Trivy version
3. **Stale OS Analyzer Import Path** - Import path changed in newer Trivy versions
4. **Incomplete Scan Scope Control** - Missing analyzer types in disabled list
5. **.NET Ecosystem Support Gaps** - Missing lockfile format mappings

**Important**: This test does NOT fix these issues. It only demonstrates and validates their existence.

## Files Included

- **regression_test.go** - The main regression test file (18KB)
- **REGRESSION_TEST_SUMMARY.md** - Detailed documentation of all issues
- **REGRESSION_TEST_FINDINGS.md** - Root cause analysis and fix recommendations
- **TEST_README.md** - This file

## How to Run

```bash
go test -run TestRegression -v -timeout 60s /workspace/regression_test.go
```

### Run a Specific Sub-Test
```bash

# Test OS Analyzer import issue
go test -run TestRegression/OS_Analyzer_Import_Path_Issue -v /workspace/regression_test.go

# Test incomplete scope control
go test -run TestRegression/Incomplete_Scan_Scope_Control -v /workspace/regression_test.go

# Test .NET ecosystem issue
go test -run TestRegression/DotNET_Ecosystem_Missing_Entries -v /workspace/regression_test.go
```
